<p>"<b>You and I</b>" (stylized as "<b>Yoü and I</b>") is a song by American singer <a href="/wiki/Lady_Gaga" title="Lady Gaga">Lady Gaga</a>, taken from her second <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Studio_album" title="Studio album">studio album</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Born_This_Way_(album)" title="Born This Way (album)">Born This Way</a></i> (2011). Written by Gaga, "You and I" samples <a href="/wiki/Queen_(band)" title="Queen (band)">Queen</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/We_Will_Rock_You" title="We Will Rock You">We Will Rock You</a>" (1977) and features <a href="/wiki/Electric_guitar" title="Electric guitar">electric guitar</a> by Queen's <a href="/wiki/Brian_May" title="Brian May">Brian May</a>. Gaga debuted the song in June 2010 during her performance at <a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a>'s White Tie and Tiara Ball. Footage of the performance appeared on the Internet, and positive response encouraged her to include the song on her <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Setlist" title="Setlist">setlist</a> for <a href="/wiki/The_Monster_Ball_Tour" title="The Monster Ball Tour">The Monster Ball Tour</a>. She later performed the song on <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Today_(NBC_program)" title="Today (NBC program)">Today</a></i> to a record crowd in July 2010, and on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Oprah_Winfrey_Show" title="The Oprah Winfrey Show">The Oprah Winfrey Show</a></i> in May 2011. On August 23, 2011, Interscope released the song as the fourth single from the album.</p>
<p>"You and I" is a slow <a href="/wiki/Tempo" title="Tempo">tempo</a> song featuring instrumentation from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electric_guitars" title="Electric guitars">electric guitars</a> and piano, with Gaga and Lange providing background vocals. The song received critical acclaim, with reviewers listing it as one of the highlights from <i>Born This Way</i>. After the release of the parent album, "You and I" charted in Canada, United Kingdom and the United States, due to digital downloads from the parent album. <a href="/wiki/American_Idol_(season_10)" title="American Idol (season 10)">Season ten</a> <i><a href="/wiki/American_Idol" title="American Idol">American Idol</a></i> contestant <a href="/wiki/Haley_Reinhart" title="Haley Reinhart">Haley Reinhart</a> performed "You and I" in May 2011 before its release, earning positive reviews. Her studio recording was released to the <a href="/wiki/ITunes_Store" title="ITunes Store">iTunes Store</a> as a single, and appeared on the <a href="/wiki/Compilation_album" title="Compilation album">compilation album</a>, <i>American Idol Top 5 Season 10</i>. "You and I" was nominated for the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Pop_Solo_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Pop Solo Performance">Grammy Award for Best Pop Solo Performance</a> at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/54th_Grammy_Awards" title="54th Grammy Awards">54th Grammy Awards</a>, which was held on February 12, 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54th_Annual_Grammy_Awards_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-54th_Annual_Grammy_Awards-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>The accompanying music video for "You and I", shot by Gaga's long-time collaborator <a href="/wiki/Laurieann_Gibson" title="Laurieann Gibson">Laurieann Gibson</a> in Springfield, Nebraska, was released on August 16, 2011. It features Jo Calderone, Gaga's male alter ego, who also appears on the single's cover, and Yüyi, her <a href="/wiki/Mermaid" title="Mermaid">mermaid</a> alter ego. Gaga's journey to be with her beloved one was the main concept behind the video. She is displayed in an assortment of scenes as different avatars, including Calderone and Yuyi. The video met with a positive reception after its release.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background_and_release">Background and release</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=You_and_I_(Lady_Gaga_song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background and release">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lady_Gaga_You_and_I.jpg"><img alt="A blond woman with short cropped hair, singing to a microphone, in front of a piano. Faces of the crowd can be seen behind her." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Lady_Gaga_You_and_I.jpg/220px-Lady_Gaga_You_and_I.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Lady_Gaga_You_and_I.jpg/330px-Lady_Gaga_You_and_I.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Lady_Gaga_You_and_I.jpg/440px-Lady_Gaga_You_and_I.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lady_Gaga_You_and_I.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gaga performing "You and I" for <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Today_(NBC_program)" title="Today (NBC program)">Today</a></i> on July 9, 2010</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>"You and I", written by Lady Gaga and produced by Gaga and <a href="/wiki/Robert_John_%22Mutt%22_Lange" title='Robert John "Mutt" Lange'>Robert John "Mutt" Lange</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lange_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lange-3">[3]</a></sup> was one of the first songs previewed from the album. Gaga said she wrote the song in New York, while she was busy playing her old piano. The singer first played "You and I" at <a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a>'s White Tie and Tiara Ball in June 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-you.26_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-you.26-4">[4]</a></sup> She said that the song was a bit of a "rock-and-roll tune" and, as such, was unlikely to be released as a <a href="/wiki/Single_(music)" title="Single (music)">single</a> from <i>Born This Way</i>. She said that it " is very dear" to her heart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-you.26_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-you.26-4">[4]</a></sup> Footage of the performance appeared on the Internet soon after, and positive response encouraged Lady Gaga to perform the song during the first concert of the North American leg of <a href="/wiki/The_Monster_Ball_Tour" title="The Monster Ball Tour">The Monster Ball Tour</a> in Montreal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Montgomery_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-Montgomery-5">[5]</a></sup> Gaga told <a href="/wiki/MSNBC" title="MSNBC">MSNBC</a>'s Meredith Vieira and Ann Curry that "'You and I' was written about the most important person that I ever met",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> allegedly Lüc Carl, her ex-boyfriend.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>Gaga announced "You and I" as the fourth single from <i>Born This Way</i> on July 22, 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> Its cover, released on August 5, 2011, via <a href="/wiki/TwitPic" title="TwitPic">TwitPic</a>, was accompanied by the line: "You will never find what you are looking for in love, if you don't love yourself." It features two black-and-white images of Gaga's male alter ego Jo Calderone smoking a cigarette and sporting sideburns.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dta_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-dta-9">[9]</a></sup> The Calderone character made a previous appearance in June 2011, when Gaga posed as him in London for a series of photos by photographer <a href="/wiki/Nick_Knight_(photographer)" title="Nick Knight (photographer)">Nick Knight</a>, arranged by stylist <a href="/wiki/Nicola_Formichetti" title="Nicola Formichetti">Nicola Formichetti</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> One shot features him wearing a blazer and white T-shirt with his head down smoking a cigarette. The other image is of Jo Calderone in silhouette exhaling a cloud of smoke.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>A writer for Australia's <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph_(Australia)" title="The Daily Telegraph (Australia)">The Daily Telegraph</a></i> described the images as having a moody and scruffy look, and felt that Gaga had become "bored with being an outrageous woman and has decided to switch gender instead."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dta_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-dta-9">[9]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Rap-Up" title="Rap-Up">Rap-Up</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s David Jones commented that Gaga's Calderone character appearing on the cover looked similar to musician <a href="/wiki/Bob_Dylan" title="Bob Dylan">Bob Dylan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> Although Steve Pond of <i><a href="/wiki/Reuters" title="Reuters">Reuters</a></i> did not like the song, he stated about the artwork: "Lady Gaga loves herself even when she's dressed as a guy."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Composition">Composition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=You_and_I_(Lady_Gaga_song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Composition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="mbox-small" role="presentation" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9;">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div class="center">
<div class="floatnone"><img alt="" data-file-height="160" data-file-width="160" height="50" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/50px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/75px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/100px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></div>
</div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="line-height:1.1em">
<div class="haudio">
<div style="padding:4px 0"><a href="/wiki/File:Lady_Gaga_-_You_%26_I.ogg" title="File:Lady Gaga - You &amp; I.ogg">'You and I'</a></div>
<div>
<div class="mediaContainer" style="width:220px"><audio class="kskin" controls="" data-durationhint="29.94" data-mwprovider="local" data-mwtitle="Lady_Gaga_-_You_&amp;_I.ogg" data-startoffset="0" id="mwe_player_0" preload="none" style="width:220px">
<source data-bandwidth="63981" data-height="0" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-title="Original Ogg file (64 kbps)" data-width="0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/9/92/Lady_Gaga_-_You_%26_I.ogg" type='audio/ogg; codecs="vorbis"'></source></audio></div>
</div>
<div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0">A sample of "You and I", where Gaga sings the <a href="/wiki/Refrain" title="Refrain">bridge</a>, which includes the lines "Sit back down on the couch where we made love the first time, and you said to me", a reference to the couch on which she had made love with her boyfriend, Lüc Carl.</div>
</div>
<hr/></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="mbox-text" colspan="2" style="line-height:1.1em"><span><i>Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">media help</a>.</i></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>"You and I" has <a href="/wiki/Rock_music" title="Rock music">rock</a> and <a href="/wiki/Country_music" title="Country music">country music</a> influences,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-you.26_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-you.26-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> and features British rock band <a href="/wiki/Queen_(band)" title="Queen (band)">Queen</a>'s guitarist <a href="/wiki/Brian_May" title="Brian May">Brian May</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-May_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-May-15">[15]</a></sup> It was <a href="/wiki/Sound_recording_and_reproduction" title="Sound recording and reproduction">recorded</a> by Tom Ware and Horace Ward at the Warehouse Productions Studio in Omaha, Nebraska, and Allertwon Hill in the United Kingdom, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-liner_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-liner-16">[16]</a></sup> Along with May, Justin Shirley Smith also played guitars; Gene Grimaldi <a href="/wiki/Audio_mastering" title="Audio mastering">mastered</a> the track. <a href="/wiki/Olle_Romo" title="Olle Romo">Olle Romo</a> did additional recording and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Music_programming" title="Music programming">programming</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-liner_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-liner-16">[16]</a></sup> Gaga teased that "someone legendary" would be producing the track before production credits were announced in April 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> Gaga, a Queen fan (even taking her <a href="/wiki/Stage_name" title="Stage name">stage name</a> from the Queen song "<a href="/wiki/Radio_Ga_Ga" title="Radio Ga Ga">Radio Ga Ga</a>"), admitted to "[falling] to the floor crying and laughing" when she found out that May agreed to the collaboration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> Lange asked Gaga to record a "rough lead vocal" for the track while she was touring. Gaga later recalled: "I had about 30 cigarettes and a couple of glasses of Jameson and just put on a click track and sang my face off, thinking we'd redo the vocals."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Offstage_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-Offstage-19">[19]</a></sup> However, Lange was satisfied with her recording and used it on the track.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Offstage_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-Offstage-19">[19]</a></sup> Ware recalled that the song was recorded the night after Gaga's March 17, 2011, concert for <a href="/wiki/The_Monster_Ball_Tour" title="The Monster Ball Tour">The Monster Ball Tour</a>. She welcomed his opinions and encouraged his input which he said helped make the four-hour session the best working experience he has had with a celebrity. "She was flattering toward the studio — and Omaha, too, for that matter. She is a bright young lady with remarkable music instincts who charts her own path," he added.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to the sheet music published by <a href="/wiki/Sony/ATV_Music_Publishing" title="Sony/ATV Music Publishing">Sony/ATV Music Publishing</a>, "You and I" is set in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Common_time" title="Common time">common time</a> with a slow <a href="/wiki/Tempo" title="Tempo">tempo</a> of 60 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beats_per_minute" title="Beats per minute">beats per minute</a>. It is written in the <a href="/wiki/Key_(music)" title="Key (music)">key</a> of <a href="/wiki/A_major" title="A major">A major</a>. During the song Gaga's voice spans from the notes of E<sub>3</sub> to C<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;">♯</span><sub>5</sub>. The song begins with an A–G–A <a href="/wiki/Chord_progression" title="Chord progression">chord progression</a>, which changes to A–Bm/A–D/A–B<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;">♯</span>m during the chorus, and back to the former chords afterwards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> The opening lyrics—"It's been a long time since I came around/ It's been a long time, but I'm back in town/ And this time, I'm not leaving without you"—describe a whiskey-breathed lover for whom she is pining. Gil Kaufman of <a href="/wiki/MTV_News" title="MTV News">MTV News</a> described it as the "tune eschewed most of her dance flavor, right down to a rollicking barrel-house piano solo." Her voice sounded like growling during the main <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Verse_(popular_music)" title="Verse (popular music)">verses</a>, where she sings the lines: "He said, 'Sit back down where you belong, in the corner of my bar with your high heels on, Sit back down on the couch where we made love the first time..."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-you.26_4-3"><a href="#cite_note-you.26-4">[4]</a></sup> Noting the differences between live performances of the song and the studio version, Neil McCormick of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Daily Telegraph</a></i> observed that the piano parts were replaced mostly by "fizzing synths, a stomping beat sampled from "We Will Rock You", thundering <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electric_guitars" title="Electric guitars">electric guitars</a> and backing vocals stacked into shimmering choral walls."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Telegraph_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-Telegraph-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Music critic Kitty Empire writing for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> described the song as an "umlaut-toting digital country power ballad" with two <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Springsteen" title="Bruce Springsteen">Bruce Springsteen</a> references: "born to run" and Nebraska.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Empire_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-Empire-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_reception">Critical reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=You_and_I_(Lady_Gaga_song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Critical reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Brian-May_with_red_special.jpg"><img alt="Greyscale image of a middle aged man, playing guitar." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="564" data-file-width="410" height="234" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Brian-May_with_red_special.jpg/170px-Brian-May_with_red_special.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Brian-May_with_red_special.jpg/255px-Brian-May_with_red_special.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Brian-May_with_red_special.jpg/340px-Brian-May_with_red_special.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Brian-May_with_red_special.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Brian_May" title="Brian May">Brian May</a>, guitarist for rock band <a href="/wiki/Queen_(band)" title="Queen (band)">Queen</a>, plays on "You and I"</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>"You and I" received acclaim from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Music_critics" title="Music critics">music critics</a>. After hearing the White Tie and Tiara Ball performance, <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'s</span> Leah Greenblatt complimented the song for its "torchy, slow-burn cabaret quality" and for lacking "<a href="/wiki/Auto-Tune" title="Auto-Tune">Auto-Tune</a>, fancy production, or performance gimmicks."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Greenblatt_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-Greenblatt-25">[25]</a></sup> McCormick, noting the differences between Gaga's live and studio versions of the song, described the studio version as "bigger, bolder and less quirkily emotive, a custom-built radio rock ballad to induce hand claps in packed stadiums. This is not music for the underground: it is cheesy, high-gloss, pop rock for the mainstream middle, a kind of instant Eighties retro classic to seduce middle-aged rockers – possibly the last demographic to remain sceptical about her appeal."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Telegraph_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-Telegraph-22">[22]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jody_Rosen" title="Jody Rosen">Jody Rosen</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> called the song a confessional power ballad "with a torrid, <a href="/wiki/Sturm_und_Drang" title="Sturm und Drang">Sturm und Drang</a> vocal turn".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> In his review for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i>, Tim Jonze said the song "aims for a 'Hey Jude' style singalong but – owing to its determination to have someone playing kitchen sink in the background – ends up as bloated as Oasis' 'All Around the World'."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> Dan Aquilante of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_New_York_Post" title="The New York Post">The New York Post</a></i> wrote a less-than-favorable review of <i><a href="/wiki/Born_This_Way_(album)" title="Born This Way (album)">Born This Way</a></i> but complimented "You and I" and the "uniquely earthy quality" that Lange brought to the album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> Kitty Empire said the song is Gaga's "unlikely heartland moment – a bid, perhaps, to locate herself as an all-American balladeer as well as an art-disco avatar with tent pegs under her skin", referring to the implants featured in the music video for the song "<a href="/wiki/Born_This_Way_(song)" title="Born This Way (song)">Born This Way</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Empire_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-Empire-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Dartmouth" title="The Dartmouth">The Dartmouth</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'s</span> Kate Sullivan wrote that "You and I" may be Gaga's most honest song to date.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dartmouth_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dartmouth-29">[29]</a></sup> Shirley Halperin of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hollywood_Reporter" title="The Hollywood Reporter">The Hollywood Reporter</a></i> wondered whether pop radio would play the song, considering Gaga's popularity. Halperin felt that the track emoted "a sense of grandness that listeners don't always get with Gaga's RedOne-produced heavily-synthetic sounds." Conversely, she felt that the live piano and background vocals by Gaga and Lange added "an undeniably lush quality, while the lyrics drives the song home and potentially into hit territory."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thr_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-thr-30">[30]</a></sup> Kerri Mason of <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> felt that the "country ballad" made no contextual sense.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> Nekesa Mumbi Moody, while reviewing <i>Born This Way</i> for <i><a href="/wiki/Florida_Today" title="Florida Today">Florida Today</a></i>, compared the song to "<a href="/wiki/Speechless_(Lady_Gaga_song)" title="Speechless (Lady Gaga song)">Speechless</a>", a similar tempo song included on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Fame_Monster" title="The Fame Monster">The Fame Monster</a></i> (2009).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Robert Copsey, a writer for the website <a href="/wiki/Digital_Spy" title="Digital Spy">Digital Spy</a> gave the song four out of five stars calling it a "torchy, retro-classic, all-American power ballad custom-built for the masses – and one we suspect Stefani would be proud to call her own."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> Amy Sciarretto of <a href="/wiki/Artistdirect" title="Artistdirect">Artistdirect</a> concluded that the song was "a bit bluesier than anything you'd expect from the dance floor icon."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/AllMusic" title="AllMusic">AllMusic</a><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Thomas_Erlewine" title="Stephen Thomas Erlewine">Stephen Thomas Erlewine</a> chose the song as a highlight on <i>Born This Way</i> saying that Gaga shows her vulnerability in it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allmusic1_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic1-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>"You and I" was nominated for <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Pop_Solo_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Pop Solo Performance">Best Pop Solo Performance</a> at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/54th_Grammy_Awards" title="54th Grammy Awards">54th Grammy Awards</a>, which was held on February 12, 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54th_Annual_Grammy_Awards_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-54th_Annual_Grammy_Awards-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Chart_performance">Chart performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=You_and_I_(Lady_Gaga_song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Chart performance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lady_Gaga_You_and_I_Manchester.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4301" data-file-width="2868" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Lady_Gaga_You_and_I_Manchester.jpg/170px-Lady_Gaga_You_and_I_Manchester.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Lady_Gaga_You_and_I_Manchester.jpg/255px-Lady_Gaga_You_and_I_Manchester.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Lady_Gaga_You_and_I_Manchester.jpg/340px-Lady_Gaga_You_and_I_Manchester.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lady_Gaga_You_and_I_Manchester.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Lady Gaga performing "You and I" in Manchester on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Born_This_Way_Ball_Tour" title="The Born This Way Ball Tour">The Born This Way Ball Tour</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the United States, "You and I" debuted on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> at number 36 on the June 11, 2011, chart having sold 83,000 downloads.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hot100debut_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-hot100debut-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbhot100_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbhot100-37">[37]</a></sup> The song re-entered the August 27, 2011, <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 at number 96, while debuting on the <a href="/wiki/Mainstream_Top_40" title="Mainstream Top 40">Pop Songs</a> chart at number 35.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-popdebut_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-popdebut-39">[39]</a></sup> The following week, the song was the greatest gainer on the digital chart, entering at number 24 having sold 56,000 copies, while moving to number 35 on the Hot 100. It also gained airplay and became the highest debuting song on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Radio_Songs" title="Radio Songs">Radio Songs</a> chart, entering at number 58 with 22 million audience impressions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> Following her performance on the MTV Video Music Awards, "You and I" moved up to number 16 on the Hot 100, with a 92% increase in digital sales to 109,000 and a 50% increase in airplay to 32 million, according to <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_Broadcast_Data_Systems" title="Nielsen Broadcast Data Systems">Nielsen Broadcast Data Systems</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> The following week, it moved to number six on the Hot 100 with a 61% increase in digital sales to 175,000 and a 32% increase in radio play to 41 million audience impressions, reaching number four and number 23 on the Digital Songs and Radio Songs charts, respectively. "You and I" became Gaga's eleventh consecutive top ten single on the Hot 100.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> In October 2011 it became Gaga's tenth song to sell 1 million in the U.S.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> As of April 2015, "You and I" has sold 2,310,000 digital downloads in the US<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UStotal_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-UStotal-44">[44]</a></sup> becoming Gaga's tenth two-million seller.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> In June 2012, "You and I" received a double platinum certification from the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a>.</p>
<p>In Canada, the song entered the Hot Digital Songs chart at number 14, subsequently debuting on the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Hot_100" title="Canadian Hot 100">Canadian Hot 100</a> at number 27.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> It entered the charts again at number 45, and has reached a peak of number 10.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-can_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-can-47">[47]</a></sup> Before the single was officially released in Australia, digital downloads were sold, consequently it entered the <a href="/wiki/ARIA_Charts" title="ARIA Charts">ARIA Singles Chart</a> at number 56 on August 15, 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ARIA_Chartifacts_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-ARIA_Chartifacts-48">[48]</a></sup> The following week, the song moved up to number 34, and has reached a peak of number 14.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aus_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-aus-49">[49]</a></sup> Following the album's release on May 23, 2011, "You and I" entered the <a href="/wiki/UK_Singles_Chart" title="UK Singles Chart">UK Singles Chart</a> at number 89, thanks to digital downloads from <i>Born This Way</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> The song jumped up to number 70 from its previous week's position of number 187, in the issue dated September 3, 2011, and has reached a peak of number 23.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uk_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-uk-51">[51]</a></sup> In Japan, the song had initially entered the digital chart at number 98, but after the MTV Video Music Awards performance, it entered the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japan_Hot_100" title="Japan Hot 100">Japan Hot 100</a> at number eight.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-riaj_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-riaj-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jap_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-jap-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_video">Music video</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=You_and_I_(Lady_Gaga_song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Music video">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=You_and_I_(Lady_Gaga_song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:30%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>It was so sweet, and I looked out and it's so beautiful, that tall corn... Then all of a sudden you start to see these monsters pop up. I love this place [Nebraska] so much, and it really comes from a genuine place. The person who I wrote this song about has been my buddy and my best friend since I was 19 years old, and he's from here.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nebraska_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-nebraska-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: left;">—Gaga talking about her love for Nebraska, and the shooting of the video.</cite></div>
<p>"You and I"'s music video was filmed in Springfield, Nebraska in July 2011, and was directed by Lady Gaga's choreographer <a href="/wiki/Laurieann_Gibson" title="Laurieann Gibson">Laurieann Gibson</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Corner_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-Corner-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> In the video, Gaga walks from New York City to Nebraska to get her boyfriend back. According to Gaga: "I'm walking with no luggage and no nothing and it's just me and my ankles are bleeding a little bit and there's grass stuck in my shoes and I've got this outfit on and it's real sort of New York clothing and I'm sprinting... And the [video is about the] idea that when you're away from someone you love, it's torture," she continued. "I knew I wanted the video to be about me sprinting back and walking hundreds of thousands of miles to get him back."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Corner_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-Corner-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>She announced that the video would be the 1,000th tweet on her Twitter account.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> Gaga confirmed to <a href="/wiki/MTV_News" title="MTV News">MTV News</a> that the video would premiere on August 18, 2011 on MTV.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> However, two days before it was to air, parts of the clip leaked on the Internet, prompting Gaga to post three tweets which, together, read "FUCK THURS DAY".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BillboardLeak_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-BillboardLeak-61">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> The messages were followed immediately by her 1,000th Twitter message: "You must love all + every part of me, as must I, for this complex + incomprehensible force to be true," including a link to the full music video, uploaded to Gaga's <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> channel two days earlier than its scheduled première.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BillboardLeak_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-BillboardLeak-61">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nydailynews-youandi-release_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-nydailynews-youandi-release-63">[63]</a></sup> The video features Gaga's two <a href="/wiki/Alter_ego" title="Alter ego">alter egos</a>: Jo Calderone, Gaga's male ego, and Yüyi, a <a href="/wiki/Mermaid" title="Mermaid">mermaid</a> she had hinted would appear in the video in July 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BillboardLeak_61-2"><a href="#cite_note-BillboardLeak-61">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following the video's premiere on MTV, Gaga explained some of the its scenes and her inspiration: "The video is quite complex in the way that the story is told, and it's meant to be slightly linear and slightly twisted and confusing, which is the way that love is." <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-expl_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-expl-65">[65]</a></sup> Regarding the sexual intercourse scenes between actor <a href="/wiki/Taylor_Kinney" title="Taylor Kinney">Taylor Kinney</a> and the singer as a mermaid, Gaga explained that it emphasized metaphorically that sometimes relationships did not work. "No matter what you do, there's this giant boundary between you and someone else. So that's what it's about, perceiving in your imagination that there's something magical inside of you that you can make it work."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-expl_65-1"><a href="#cite_note-expl-65">[65]</a></sup> After revealing that the wedding dress shown in the video belonged to her mother, Gaga explained the scenes involving the <a href="/wiki/Ice_cream_van" title="Ice cream van">ice cream truck</a>. According to her, they represented the destruction of her youth, experiences she had shared in earlier interviews.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-expl_65-2"><a href="#cite_note-expl-65">[65]</a></sup> Explaining her decision to include them, Gaga said:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>That's how I wanted to open the video, because I think it really sets up the rest of the story. It allows you to imagine you yourself are not just one person; you're so many. That person has so many stories and memories to draw from, and they all affect your journey profusely. I'm battered quite brutally at the beginning of the video, but at the end, I'm not battered; I'm a bit strange. It's not meant to be an answer video; it's meant to be a profuse number of the question.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-expl_65-3"><a href="#cite_note-expl-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Synopsis">Synopsis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=You_and_I_(Lady_Gaga_song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Synopsis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GagaYuyi.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="255" data-file-width="600" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/36/GagaYuyi.jpg/300px-GagaYuyi.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/36/GagaYuyi.jpg/450px-GagaYuyi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/3/36/GagaYuyi.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:GagaYuyi.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Lady Gaga as Yuyi the Mermaid in the music video</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The music video begins with Gaga, dressed in black clothing, sunglasses, bloody feet, and seemingly bionic features, walking through a field in Nebraska; having returned on foot after years of absence. Gaga goes to buy ice cream from an ice cream truck, but she suddenly drops it as a toothless man with a <a href="/wiki/Doll" title="Doll">doll</a> in his hand grins at her. She begins to have flashbacks to an earlier time spent in Nebraska as scenes of Gaga having a wedding, being tortured by a man inside a barn, and being inside a <a href="/wiki/Water_tank" title="Water tank">water tank</a> appear in quick succession. The song starts playing as the camera zooms slowly towards Gaga, who is standing bent forward as she begins singing. The video continually switches to scenes where Gaga, with little make up, a simple gray-colored hair style, and a white dress, plays a <a href="/wiki/Piano" title="Piano">piano</a> in the middle of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cornfield" title="Cornfield">cornfield</a>, while her male alter ego, Jo Calderone, sits on top of the piano, smoking and drinking a beer. As Calderone pulls up his sleeves, present day Gaga is still walking through the desert.</p>
<p>During the second verse, a mad scientist, portrayed by Kinney, seemingly tortures Gaga, who is wearing a yellow dress with glasses made of barbwire, as another version of the singer, with teal-colored hair, performs a dance routine with her <a href="/wiki/Backup_dancer" title="Backup dancer">backup dancers</a> in a barn. As the chorus begins for the second time, Gaga appears as Yüyi the Mermaid, with gills on her face and neck, as she lies in a tub filled with dirty water. At the end of the chorus, the camera zooms to a brunette Gaga inside a water tank while she sings "You and I" in the desert scene, and in the cornfield with Calderone. Interspersing scenes again show Gaga having her wedding, Yüyi in her tub, and Gaga seated on a chair with a <a href="/wiki/Conveyor_belt" title="Conveyor belt">conveyor belt</a>. During May's guitar solo, Gaga dances in the cornfield with other dancers dressed in the same white dress, as Yüyi and the scientist kiss. While singing the chorus for the final time, Gaga kisses Calderone in one sequence and runs across the field in another. As the video reaches its conclusion, the tortured Gaga is being slid down as the conveyor belt turns on. The video ends with Yüyi and the scientist together in the bath tub, as a depiction of their dream wedding flashes across, before a last shot of the barn as the screen turns black.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=You_and_I_(Lady_Gaga_song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Following its premature release on the Web, the music video for "You and I" met with positive reviews. Matthew Perpetua of <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> felt the video was an improvement over her earlier videos, <i><a href="/wiki/Judas_(Lady_Gaga_song)" title="Judas (Lady Gaga song)">Judas</a></i> and <i>The Edge of Glory</i>, saying, "the best moments of the video put a distinctly Gaga-ish spin on the iconography of Americana and traditional love stories."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> Jillian Mapes of <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> wrote the video has: "torture contraptions, mermaid sex, a wedding, bondage in a barn, an ice cream truck, and to top it all off, 'Children of the Corn' and religious overtones thrown in for good measure," and thought the video setting was the strangest representation of Nebraska.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BillboardLeak_61-3"><a href="#cite_note-BillboardLeak-61">[61]</a></sup> Leah Collins of <i><a href="/wiki/Dose_(magazine)" title="Dose (magazine)">Dose</a></i> felt the video was a "great opportunity for the singer to finally find out what it's like to make out with herself."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> Kyle Anderson of <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i> noted of the scene in which Gaga plays a piano in a cornfield beside her male alter ego: "She's just Stefani Joanne Angelina Germanotta, playing a piano in the middle of a corn field—with a little making out on the side, of course."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> Gil Kaufman of MTV News believed that Gaga was not joking when she talked about the video being about the "torture" of being away from the one you love. "And, man, based on the bruising final product, she wasn't kidding," Kaufman concluded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nebraska_54-1"><a href="#cite_note-nebraska-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>Jocelyn Vena of MTV found influences of Gaga's past videos in the various avatars she plays <i>You and I</i>. She explained that:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>when [Gaga] stands at a crossroads in a big hat, the image is reminiscent of '<a href="/wiki/Telephone_(song)" title="Telephone (song)">Telephone</a>' Gaga. When she sits nearly makeup-free at her piano in the cornfields, there are touches of the teary-eyed makeup-less Gaga from the '<a href="/wiki/Bad_Romance" title="Bad Romance">Bad Romance</a>' video. Flashes of her wedding may remind fans of the wedding dress she wore in the 'Judas' clip. Robot Gaga's facial structures recall some of the steampunk looks of her '<a href="/wiki/Alejandro_(song)" title="Alejandro (song)">Alejandro</a>' video. Those are only a few of the nods to past personae from her own videography.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>Devin Brown of <a href="/wiki/CBS_News" title="CBS News">CBS News</a> felt that Gaga had finally returned to form with the video. "After some visually pleasing but generally lackluster videos, she has finally come out with something to write home about. 'You and I' is arguably the best song on her sophomore release, <i>Born This Way</i>, and now has a video to match."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Slant_Magazine" title="Slant Magazine">Slant Magazine</a> writer commented that the publication had a mixed reaction to the video, saying that it "is essentially a collection of disconnected images we couldn't make heads or tails of."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fashion_films">Fashion films</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=You_and_I_(Lady_Gaga_song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Fashion films">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On September 1, 2011, Gaga announced on her Twitter account that she had shot five "fashion films" related to the song's music video with Dutch photographers Inez van Lamsweerde and Vinoodh Matadin. The characters are: Jo Calderone (Gaga's alter ego), Yuyi (a mermaid), Nymph, Bride, and finally Barn Hooker and Mother.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ff_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-ff-72">[72]</a></sup> After the tweet, Gaga released the first video, titled <i>Haus of Ü Featuring Nymph</i>. The two-minute black-and-white video featured Gaga with minimal make-up, wearing a short dress, performing ballet choreography. As wind blows around her, the singer looks intently toward the camera, with the parting shot in color.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ff_72-1"><a href="#cite_note-ff-72">[72]</a></sup> The second video featured her as the bride from the opening sequence of the music video. The fashion film portrayed her in the same costume, gradually removing it and her wig. At the end, she is topless with her hand covering her breasts. Interspersed between are scenes portraying people dressed like Gaga, and appearances by Taylor Kinney, who was in the music video, and the singer's stylist <a href="/wiki/Nicola_Formichetti" title="Nicola Formichetti">Nicola Formichetti</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> The third fashion film portrayed the singer as the mermaid Yüyi. She sits in a director's chair, flopping her tail. It also shows two crew members carrying Yuyi toward the barn, where the music video was filmed. Formichetti also makes a cameo in this video.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Live_performances">Live performances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=You_and_I_(Lady_Gaga_song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Live performances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lady_Gaga_-_VMA_2011_cropped.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1171" data-file-width="832" height="239" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Lady_Gaga_-_VMA_2011_cropped.jpg/170px-Lady_Gaga_-_VMA_2011_cropped.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Lady_Gaga_-_VMA_2011_cropped.jpg/255px-Lady_Gaga_-_VMA_2011_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Lady_Gaga_-_VMA_2011_cropped.jpg/340px-Lady_Gaga_-_VMA_2011_cropped.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lady_Gaga_-_VMA_2011_cropped.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Lady Gaga, as her alter ego Jo Calderone, at the <a href="/wiki/2011_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="2011 MTV Video Music Awards">2011 MTV Video Music Awards</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the first performance of "You and I" at <a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a>'s White Tie and Tiara Ball, Gaga performed the song live on the television program <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Today_(NBC_program)" title="Today (NBC program)">Today</a></i> on July 9, 2010, before an estimated crowd of 18,000–20,000 people, the largest ever to pack <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rockefeller_Plaza" title="Rockefeller Plaza">Rockefeller Plaza</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-D_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-D-75">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wieselman_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wieselman-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Celizic_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-Celizic-77">[77]</a></sup> It was next performed on the July 31, 2010, Phoenix stop of the Monster Ball Tour, where Gaga protested Arizona's immigration law <a href="/wiki/Arizona_SB_1070" title="Arizona SB 1070">SB 1070</a>—which mandates that state police officers "question any person they suspect to be an illegal immigrant and imprison any aliens not carrying one of four allowed forms of proper identification"—and dedicated her performance of "You and I" to a boy whose family had been affected by the law.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kreps_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kreps-78">[78]</a></sup> Gaga performed the album version of the track on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Oprah_Winfrey_Show" title="The Oprah Winfrey Show">The Oprah Winfrey Show</a></i> on May 5, 2011, using a piano constructed from a wire high-heel structure while sitting on a high stool.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oprah_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-Oprah-79">[79]</a></sup> The "less organic" version for the final "Harpo Hookups" episode featured an <a href="/wiki/Electric_guitar" title="Electric guitar">electric guitar</a> and modified lyrics to include <a href="/wiki/Oprah_Winfrey" title="Oprah Winfrey">Oprah</a>'s name.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>The song was on the set list of the <a href="/wiki/HBO" title="HBO">HBO</a> television special, <i><a href="/wiki/Lady_Gaga_Presents_the_Monster_Ball_Tour:_At_Madison_Square_Garden" title="Lady Gaga Presents the Monster Ball Tour: At Madison Square Garden">Lady Gaga Presents the Monster Ball Tour: At Madison Square Garden</a></i>, which aired originally on May 7, 2011, in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> Gaga's performance of "You and I" from the HBO special aired on <i><a href="/wiki/American_Idol" title="American Idol">American Idol</a></i>, the night after she mentored the four remaining contestants, and the week following <a href="/wiki/Haley_Reinhart" title="Haley Reinhart">Haley Reinhart</a>'s performance of the song.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> She performed a jazz version of "You and I" at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Radio_1%27s_Big_Weekend" title="Radio 1's Big Weekend">Radio 1's Big Weekend</a> in Carlisle, Cumbria on May 18, 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> The third performance of the album version of the song was on the <i><a href="/wiki/Paul_O%27Grady_Live" title="Paul O'Grady Live">Paul O'Grady Live</a></i> show in London, on June 17, 2011. Wearing a dress by the late <a href="/wiki/Gianni_Versace" title="Gianni Versace">Gianni Versace</a>, Gaga perched atop a New York City-inspired fire escape, where she sang the song. Ryan Love of <a href="/wiki/Digital_Spy" title="Digital Spy">Digital Spy</a> had a preview of the show's recording, and said that it was a "real treat" to hear Gaga sing the song.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-paul_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-paul-86">[86]</a></sup> In August 2011, Gaga performed "You and I" on the American TV talk show program <i><a href="/wiki/The_View_(U.S._TV_series)" title="The View (U.S. TV series)">The View</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> On August 28, 2011, Gaga attended the <a href="/wiki/2011_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="2011 MTV Video Music Awards">2011 MTV Video Music Awards</a> dressed as Jo Calderone. As Calderone, she opened the show with a four-minute monologue, explaining his broken relationship with Gaga. Following the monologue, joined on stage by Brian May, she performed "You and I".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Calderone_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-Calderone-88">[88]</a></sup> On October 6, 2011, she filmed a pre-recorded interview and performance for the single on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Jonathan_Ross_Show" title="The Jonathan Ross Show">The Jonathan Ross Show</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> Later, on October 16, 2011, she performed the song during a concert at the <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Bowl" title="Hollywood Bowl">Hollywood Bowl</a> in Los Angeles for the <a href="/wiki/Clinton_Foundation" title="Clinton Foundation">Clinton Foundation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p>On the <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">ABC</a> special, <i><a href="/wiki/A_Very_Gaga_Thanksgiving" title="A Very Gaga Thanksgiving">A Very Gaga Thanksgiving</a></i>, the singer performed the song backed by a "piano-and-trumpet arrangement".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> On November 30, during the <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">CBS</a> special titled <i>The Grammy Nominations Concert Live! – Countdown to Music's Biggest Night</i>—where the nominations for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/54th_Grammy_Awards" title="54th Grammy Awards">54th Grammy Awards</a> were revealed—Gaga performed "You and I" along with <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Nettles" title="Jennifer Nettles">Jennifer Nettles</a> of the country band <a href="/wiki/Sugarland" title="Sugarland">Sugarland</a> while <a href="/wiki/Kristian_Bush" title="Kristian Bush">Kristian Bush</a> played the guitar. During the performance, she changed the lyrics to fit the occasion: "With your high cowboy boots on. Oh Sugarland, it's been six whole years."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cbsspecial_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-cbsspecial-92">[92]</a></sup> According to James Montgomery of MTV News, she performed a "husky, musky version" of "You and I".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cbsspecial_92-1"><a href="#cite_note-cbsspecial-92">[92]</a></sup> She performed the song playing piano on her 2012 <a href="/wiki/Born_This_Way_Ball" title="Born This Way Ball">Born This Way Ball</a> tour. Like previous concert tours, the piano, fused to a motorcycle, was an elaborate prop that tied into the theme of her show. In keeping with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hair_metal" title="Hair metal">hair metal</a> theme of <i>Born This Way</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cover_versions">Cover versions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=You_and_I_(Lady_Gaga_song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Cover versions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Prior to the release of <i>Born This Way</i>, <a href="/wiki/American_Idol_(season_10)" title="American Idol (season 10)">season ten</a> <i><a href="/wiki/American_Idol" title="American Idol">American Idol</a></i> contestant <a href="/wiki/Haley_Reinhart" title="Haley Reinhart">Haley Reinhart</a> sang "You and I" as one of two performances for the "Songs from Now and Then" episode.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reinhart_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reinhart-94">[94]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Iovine" title="Jimmy Iovine">Jimmy Iovine</a>, head of Gaga's <a href="/wiki/Record_label" title="Record label">record label</a>, asked for the song and Reinhart received her permission before the performance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reinhart_94-1"><a href="#cite_note-Reinhart-94">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> Reviews of Reinhart's performance were mostly positive. Len Melisurgo of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Star-Ledger" title="The Star-Ledger">The Star-Ledger</a></i> considered it a risky choice, since the song had not been released, but accepted that Reinhart "sounded amazing" by hitting "some really high notes".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Brian_Mansfield" title="Brian Mansfield">Brian Mansfield</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a></i> described Reinhart's performance as an "old-fashioned dance-hall groove, kind of like a mid-'70s Elton John number. It's perfectly suited to that slippery growl that such a distinctive part of Haley's style. By the end of the song, she turns it into a gospel-style rocker, and she takes it to the house." Mansfield also noted that the <i>American Idol</i> judges—<a href="/wiki/Randy_Jackson" title="Randy Jackson">Randy Jackson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Lopez" title="Jennifer Lopez">Jennifer Lopez</a> and <a href="/wiki/Steven_Tyler" title="Steven Tyler">Steven Tyler</a>—reacted positively to it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> On the contrary, Jim Farber of the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Daily_News_(New_York)" title="Daily News (New York)">New York Daily News</a></i> considered the choice risky and was thankful when Reinhart performed a more familiar song for her second round.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> On May 5, 2011, Reinhart's studio recording of "You and I" was released as a digital <a href="/wiki/Single_(music)" title="Single (music)">single</a> to the <a href="/wiki/ITunes_Store" title="ITunes Store">iTunes Store</a>, and appeared on the <a href="/wiki/Compilation_album" title="Compilation album">compilation album</a> <i>American Idol Top 5 Season 10</i>. Mansfield, who initially had misgivings about Reinhart as a singer, complimented her studio recording of the track, feeling that if she could "get another 10 songs this good when it comes time to cut the record, then all my initial misgivings about this girl will vanish into thin air."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<p>British singer <a href="/wiki/Amelia_Lily" title="Amelia Lily">Amelia Lily</a> covered the song in November 2011 during her time on UK talent show <i><a href="/wiki/The_X_Factor_(UK_series_8)" title="The X Factor (UK series 8)">The X Factor</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> On November 15, 2011, comedy-drama, musical TV series <i><a href="/wiki/Glee_(TV_series)" title="Glee (TV series)">Glee</a></i> featured a mash-up of Gaga's "You and I" and <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Rabbitt" title="Eddie Rabbitt">Eddie Rabbitt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crystal_Gayle" title="Crystal Gayle">Crystal Gayle</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/You_and_I_(Eddie_Rabbitt_and_Crystal_Gayle_song)" title="You and I (Eddie Rabbitt and Crystal Gayle song)">You and I</a>", performed by <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Morrison" title="Matthew Morrison">Matthew Morrison</a> and <a href="/wiki/Idina_Menzel" title="Idina Menzel">Idina Menzel</a> (as their respective characters <a href="/wiki/Will_Schuester" title="Will Schuester">Will Schuester</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shelby_Corcoran" title="Shelby Corcoran">Shelby Corcoran</a>) in the episode "<a href="/wiki/Mash_Off" title="Mash Off">Mash Off</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ZapFri_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-ZapFri-101">[101]</a></sup> The mash-up sold 23,000 digital downloads, and debuted on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> chart at number 69, in the issue dated December 3, 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Year-end_charts">Year-end charts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=You_and_I_(Lady_Gaga_song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Year-end charts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="wikitable sortable plainrowheaders">
<tr>
<th scope="col">Chart (2011)</th>
<th scope="col">Position</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Canadian Hot 100<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></th>
